Shanghai Municipal Council's Vehicle Committee Reports on the Recent Situation of Rickshaw Pullers 101

According to the report of the Shanghai Municipal Council Rickshaw Affairs Committee, the issuance of licenses for public rickshaw pullers officially ended on October 15. Since that day, only those who had been temporarily rejected before have been processed. As of November 4, the total number of licensed rickshaw pullers in the concession was 41,098. Recently, although various rickshaw owners have repeatedly stated to the committee that there is a shortage of rickshaw pullers, the committee's investigation found that there are no vehicles idle due to a shortage of rickshaw pullers at various rickshaw owners. At the same time, it is very clear that the competition among rickshaw pullers to rent vehicles is not as enthusiastic as before, and the number of people hiring rickshaws is not as many as before. This is probably due to the economic downturn. Therefore, the fares earned by rickshaw pullers are not as high as before, and it takes more effort to negotiate the price. The Vehicle Committee deeply feels that if rickshaw owners can understand the current difficulties and reduce the rental price, the rickshaw pullers will definitely be more eager to rent vehicles. Furthermore, since the beginning of this month, there have been 501 new-style rickshaws on the market. It is expected that by the end of this year, the number of new-style vehicles will increase to 1,000. From this, it can be seen that the number of passengers who support new rickshaws is increasing. In addition, the effectiveness of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society is also becoming increasingly apparent. The society recently rented a spacious house on Machen Road as the West District branch. It is expected that the work of the society will improve from this. In addition, two rickshaw puller representatives of the society have also been elected.

Appeal of Pig Merchants in Northern Jiangsu: Requesting Jiangsu Surveillance Commissioner to Thoroughly Investigate Illegal Tax Collection 103

The business tax on pigs in northern Jiangsu, with checkpoints set up along the way and illegal and harsh taxes levied, has been repeatedly reported by the Shanghai Fresh Pork Selling Industry Association and others. Now, dozens of pig merchants in the fourth district of Bingcha, Dongtai, including Zhang Yiyuan, Fu Xuegao, Zhang Liufu, Ye Shouyu, Shen Shumin, Sha Wenxuan, Cong Yixing, and Wu Guoqing, have jointly filed a complaint with the Jiangsu Surveillance Commissioner's Office. The original text is excerpted as follows: "We merchants, since being disturbed by the Red Bandits, followed by frequent floods and droughts, the rural areas have gone bankrupt and have no way to make a living. Fortunately, we rely on agricultural by-products, transporting pigs, to survive and maintain a meager living. In May of this year, the Director of the Dongtai Business Tax Bureau arbitrarily set up a tax checkpoint at the Jiaoxie Bingcha place, using Tao Daxing Zhahe to intercept pig boats and force them to pay taxes, collecting 20 cents for each pig. They even issued private notes, deceiving and extorting, doing everything they could. If their wishes were not met, they would be detained. Unable to swallow their anger, they mortgaged their property to report. We merchants have been abused repeatedly and have suffered multiple calamities. This year's floods are severe, and most families are impoverished. Starvation is widespread. How can our livelihood at the end of the road bear such harsh taxes? Moreover, the pig transportation business tax in northern Jiangsu, with Bao Ban Tong such as the two county business taxes, Mo Zuotang, setting up tax checkpoints in Dingyan, Baipu, Matang, Liqiao, Maqiao, and other places, densely packed like forests, all kinds of illegal and harsh abuses, cannot be described. We have appealed to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to report the situation and request relief from the commercial difficulties, and we have presented it to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance for a quick investigation. We then received an order from the Ministry of Finance to strictly correct the situation and again requested your office to send personnel to thoroughly investigate the matter. Several months have passed, and the documents are full, but the harsh pig transportation business tax in northern Jiangsu has not been reduced. Instead, the Dongtai Business Tax Jiaoxie Bingcha tax checkpoint has forcibly levied taxes. On August 29, after paying the pig tax at the Dongtai Bingcha tax checkpoint, on August 30, after passing the Dingyan tax checkpoint in Rugao, 40 miles away, the tax should have been exempted upon verification of the ticket. How could the tax checkpoint consider the Dongtai tax ticket invalid and require another payment of the pig tax? Within the same jurisdiction, this tax, that tax, actually collects taxes repeatedly along the way, even more harmful than the former Likin tax. The suffering of our pig merchants is even more indescribable. Our Jiangsu is the capital province, admired by China and foreign countries, and relied on by the whole country. Unfortunately, if each Director of the Business Tax Bureau considers the difficulties of our merchants who are forced to pay taxes for their livelihood, we will again weep and continue to present this, attaching it to your Honorable Chief for verification, imploring you to show pity, relieve the commercial difficulties, and quickly send personnel to thoroughly investigate and severely punish the illegal Dongtai Tongru Directors of the Business Tax Bureau, and order the immediate abolition of the tax checkpoints along the way that are illegally collecting and extorting taxes, in order to maintain the law and save the people. We are extremely anxiously awaiting orders."

New Chinese Weights and Measures System to be Implemented in the International Settlement; Shanghai Municipal Council Passes Resolution to Implement on New Year's Day Next Year 108

The Shanghai Municipal Council believes that since the new Chinese weights and measures system was officially promulgated in 1929, it has long been implemented outside the concession with remarkable results. Now that the time is ripe, in order to show Chinese-concession cooperation, it is planned to start with adopting the standard weighing system and gradually seek the unification of weights and measures. The concession authorities plan to stipulate during the trial period that the new municipal scale should be prepared first, in order to gradually implement it. However, in order to achieve uniformity, the Municipal Council plans to issue a notice first, and afterwards, the authorities may not recognize anything other than the new municipal scale, in order to show a warning. After discussions among the various departments of the Municipal Council, it was proposed that the Police Committee recommend the following two points to the board of directors: (1) It is stipulated that whether the Shanghai Municipal Council establishes or private individuals establish vegetable markets, bakeries, candy stores, foreign food stores, vegetable stores, fruit stalls, rice stores, etc., they must all indicate on their licenses that standard new weights must be prepared by themselves. This regulation will be implemented from January 1 of the following year. (2) Issue a notice to warn all stalls that the Shanghai Municipal Council may prohibit the use of other weighing systems after six months. The Shanghai Municipal Council Police Committee has now recommended to the board of directors that this new regulation be indicated on the licenses of all vegetable markets and the above-mentioned shops, and that each stall prepare the standard municipal scale promulgated by the Chinese government. At the same time, a notice will be issued to indicate the possibility of adopting the standard new system. It is heard that the above points were all approved at the regular meeting of the board of directors the other day.

Women's Groups Petition the Fifth National Congress: Issue an Order to Effectively Prohibit Prostitution 109

And formulate a constitution based on the principle of equality between men and women

Dagon News Agency stated that the Shanghai Chinese Women's Temperance Association and the Chinese Women's Association jointly telegraphed the Fifth National Congress yesterday, requesting that an order be issued to the whole country to effectively prohibit prostitution and formulate a constitution based on the principle of equality between men and women. The original texts of the two telegrams are recorded as follows:

Telegram One

The Fifth National Congress in Nanjing: Upon investigation, the prostitution business is not only morally corrupt and depraved, but also inhumane. It leads to individual degradation on a small scale and national demise on a large scale. Therefore, all civilized countries prohibit it. Even in China before the Spring and Autumn period, there was no mention of prostitution. It can be known that the prevalence of prostitution is not allowed in a prosperous age. Since the reform of our country, although prostitution has been banned through repeated orders, those who ban ban, and those who prostitute still prostitute. This association is heartbroken and specially jointly telegraphed, asking the conference to propose and resolve to issue an order to the whole country to effectively prohibit prostitution, and to set up relief agencies as soon as possible,授and授give them living skills, so that they can seek self-reliance to rectify social customs and revitalize the nation. I cannot express my earnest anticipation.

Telegram Two

The Fifth National Congress in Nanjing: Upon investigation, equality between men and women is a common practice in modern civilized countries, and valuing men over women is a barbaric custom. All family tragedies and social disputes are mostly due to the habit of valuing men over women, which is the step to disaster. Moreover, women account for half of the entire nation. If we want to seek national rejuvenation, how can we abandon this half of the women? Therefore, in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy, the stipulations in politics, economy, law, and education are based on the principle of equality between men and women. All our compatriots should follow the conference, as representatives of the whole people, looked up to by the whole country, and relied on by all. The people's pain is waiting to be relieved, and national rejuvenation depends on leadership. For this reason, we jointly telegraphed, asking the conference to follow the previous situation, formulate a constitution based on the principle of equality between men and women, in order to prevent the former evils and show fairness, which is not only the blessing of women across the country, but also the blessing of the country's future.

Pudong Ice Factory Field Robbery and Murder Case: Chen Hegao Sentenced to Death, Lu and Liu Sentenced to Ten Months Each 110

He Desheng's small cigarette and paper shop, located at No. 71 Bingchang Field, Dongchang Road, Pudong, was broken into and robbed on August 8th of this year at 9:00 PM. He's wife, He Wangshi (25 years old, from Changzhou), resisted and shouted for help, whereupon the robbers opened fire, hitting He Wangshi in the temple, killing her instantly. The local bailiff, Lu Shunlong, reported the incident to the Procuratorate of the District Court, who dispatched personnel to inspect the scene, confirm the death, and arrange for the coffin and burial. Subsequently, the police arrested the following suspects: Chen Hegao, 33 years old, from Changzhou; Lu Jiwen, 26 years old, from Kunshan; and Liu Jinyuan, 41 years old, from Changzhou. They also seized a handgun and seven bullets. The case was handed over to the District Court, where Prosecutor Zhang Zi conducted several thorough interrogations and confirmed the facts. He also summoned the victim, He Desheng, who identified Chen Hegao as the one who held the handgun during the robbery and behaved ferociously. As a result, Chen Hegao was prosecuted for robbery and murder in the Criminal Court. Presiding Judge Cai Dingcheng held a public trial and rendered a final verdict yesterday at 10:00 AM, sentencing Chen Hegao to death for robbery and murder, and sentencing Lu and Liu to ten months imprisonment each as a warning. Chen Hegao refused to accept the verdict and declared his intention to appeal. Lu and Liu accepted the verdict and were ordered to be remanded in custody pending further instructions.

Decline of Social Morals is Worrying: Elder Brother Sells Younger Sister into Prostitution, Sister Flees Back from Qingdao, Brother Apprehended and Sent for Investigation 111

Jin Jindi, a 16-year-old girl from Funing, with some good looks, lived in a bungalow on Longjiang Road. She was a worker at the Weitong Yarn Factory on Lan Road. On December 20th of last year, her elder brother, Jin Rutian, colluded with Gao Xiaobao, a female foreman at the factory, to sell her to a brothel in Qingdao under the pretext of going to work there, earning 300 yuan, which they divided and spent. Her mother, Jin Liushi, searched without success after her daughter went missing, unaware of her brother's involvement. In the brothel, Jin Jindi primarily entertained Westerners. After two weeks, unaccustomed to this kind of promiscuity, she obtained the madam's consent and wrote a letter to Shanghai, asking her mother to prepare 200 yuan to redeem her from Qingdao. Jin Liushi went to Qingdao with the money on several occasions to negotiate with the madam, Zhu Xiaozhen. However, because the amount she brought was insufficient, she had to return to Shanghai, unable to raise the funds. Recently, Jin Jindi seized an opportunity to flee back from Qingdao. The day before yesterday, at 6:00 PM, she and her mother encountered her brother, Jin Rutian, near Pingliang Road and Qiqihar Road. They seized him and began to quarrel. Detective Jin Wanrong saw the commotion, inquired about the details, arrested him, and took him to the Yulin Road police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The lawyer from the Municipal Council, Zhang Shizhu, detailed the previous events and stated that the defendant denied the allegations at the police station, requesting an extension. Following this, Jin Liushi and her daughter Jin Jindi testified to the events, questioning the defendant, whose answers were evasive. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered him to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing to investigate further.

Pudong: Fire Brigade Adds Fire Engine 115

Zhao Longsheng, the director of the Pudong Fire Brigade, believed that the fire engines currently in use were outdated and the water pressure was too weak. This made it difficult to put out large fires. Therefore, he submitted a request to the Municipal Public Security Bureau last year to purchase a new large fire engine, which was commissioned to the Hengda Fire Engine Manufacturing Factory, a Chinese business located at the southern end of the Laolaji Bridge. The fire engine was recently completed. Yesterday morning, Director Zhao, accompanied by the driver, drove the engine out of the factory, passed through the North Bund of China Merchants, hired a tugboat to transport it to the Blue Chimney Pier in Pudong, and drove it back to the fire brigade. The engine is 26 and a half feet long, eight feet wide, and weighs three and a half tons. It is equipped with two main water outlets and six branch outlets, with a water pressure of 350 gallons per minute, and a range of 160 feet high and 180 feet far. It also has a small pump with a water pressure of 100 feet. The engine speed is 40 miles per hour. The engine is equipped with a three-section ladder, which can reach 48 feet high. The entire engine, except for the engine itself, was manufactured by Chinese, and is worth over 10,000 yuan. During the test run yesterday afternoon, the results were very satisfactory. It is reported that the fire brigade will invite people from all walks of life to visit this Saturday afternoon.

Central Bank Inspection Report 121

The 256th inspection report on the issue reserve of Central Bank convertible notes states: In accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, the committee is responsible for inspecting the amount of convertible notes issued by the bank and the reserve. The 256th inspection was held at the Issuing Bureau of the bank on November 9th, 1935, and the results are reported as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible notes issued: 139,815,034 silver dollars, including 127,729,454 silver dollar notes and 12,085,580 subsidiary currency notes. Total amount of convertible note reserve: 139,815,034 silver dollars, including 94,566,634 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 77,719,282 yuan in the bank's issuing vault, 1,020,000 yuan in the issuing branch, 2,426,929 yuan in various branches, and 13,929,423 yuan in deposits with other banks. The security reserve is equivalent to 45,248,400 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued: 586,679.80 customs gold units. Total amount of customs gold convertible note reserve: 586,679.80 customs gold units. This reserve includes 11,553.59 taels of gold bullion, at a fixed price of 5.0779, equivalent to 586,679.80 customs gold units. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the remainder must be security reserves of legal quality. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the security reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This is reported accordingly. November 11th, 1935. Li Fusun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jilun.

Countries such as Calcutta in India, Kobe in Japan, and Rotterdam in the Netherlands have also placed orders one after another. As a result, the demand for domestic glycerin exceeds supply. Recently, domestic and foreign sales have increased even more. It is expected that if production can be increased, exports will be even more active. This is indeed the first case of a domestic scientific material being promoted abroad.

Letters Received

The Path of Political Reform (Continued) (November 1935, Shanghai) 127

-- Respectfully dedicated to the comrades of the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang and gentlemen who are fond of discussing political reform --

Third, whether the national crisis can be resolved depends entirely on whether the entire nation, from top to bottom, can be of one heart and one mind and work diligently to fulfill their duties, and it can be said to be completely unrelated to whether party rule is abolished or whether political tutelage is ended. The current international environment no longer allows us to live our lives perfunctorily. If everyone, from the leader to the masses, can truly work hard, I do not believe that the national crisis will remain serious forever, nor do I believe that the nation will ultimately fail to revive. On the other hand, if party rule is abolished, allowing many political parties to compete and contend, and political tutelage is ended, allowing parliamentarians elected through bribery to make trouble in parliament and obstruct the government, will the national crisis not become even more serious? Will the people's livelihood revive as a result? Jiang Tingfu claims to have no affection for the Kuomintang, but he rightly said in the Tianjin Dagong Bao: "The people do not care who holds power; what they hope is that those in power can do a few major things for the country and the people." Therefore, a government of party rule or a government of political tutelage, if it can relieve the national crisis for the country and the people, will certainly be loved by the people no less than a democratic government or a constitutional government. On the other hand, if a democratic or constitutional government cannot resolve the national crisis, the people will certainly abandon it, and a government of party rule or political tutelage may one day reappear. The fact that the German National Socialist Party was able to overthrow the Brüning government and organize a one-party dictatorship government under the Weimar Constitution shows this. Jiang Tingfu also said: "Those who oppose Chiang, if they think their cause will succeed, the foreign threat will naturally stop, this is a dream. Or if they think that even if it does not stop, they will have the power to resist Japan once they gain power, this is deceiving people." This is truly speaking plainly. Those who currently oppose the Kuomintang gnash their teeth and believe that as long as they overthrow the Kuomintang's party rule and end the Kuomintang's political tutelage, the national crisis will naturally be resolved. He is either dreaming or deceiving people. (To be continued)

General Situation of Shanghai's Textile Industry (Continued) Compiled by China Credit Information Agency (One of the General Situations of Shanghai Industry and Commerce) 3. The Actual Situation of Shanghai's Yarn Sales in Recent Years 128

To understand the major changes in Shanghai's yarn industry in recent years, it is necessary to start from its production and sales, and the slow rise and fall of yarn and cotton prices. According to statistics from the Chinese Yarn Mill Association, the number of yarn bales produced by various mills has increased slightly in the past three years, with 640,000 bales in 1932, 650,000 bales in 1933, and 670,000 bales in 1934. There are no overall figures for the first three quarters of this year. As for the increase or decrease in sales, it can be inferred from the growth or decline in the number of spot yarn transactions by various broker groups in the Shanghai Yarn and Cloth Exchange:

Table of Spot Yarn Transaction Volume of Various Broker Groups in Shanghai in Recent Three Years (Original Unit: Bales)

1933 1934 1935

January -- 17,636 17,569

February -- 11,390 19,071

March 13,801 13,680 46,104

April 28,878 26,376 24,886

May 20,352 37,235 25,516

June 19,507 27,826 26,691

July 27,163 26,056 27,811

August 15,754 32,149 21,938

September 22,134 35,858 31,085

October 27,548 42,773 --

November 20,238 33,428 --

December 11,369 34,068 --

Monthly Average 26,674 28,206 26,741

In terms of annual data, the customer sales situation this year is slightly worse than last year, but compared with the previous year, it is still slightly better. In terms of monthly data, customer sales in March this year were particularly strong, increasing by more than 30,000 bales compared to last year and the year before, so after March, they turned downwards, and then became strong again in September. Overall, customer sales in each month of the first three quarters of this year were more than the same period in the previous year, and there were also ups and downs compared with the same period last year, so the future prospects may be promising.

The accumulation of stockpiled yarn is indeed one of the important symptoms of Shanghai's yarn industry during a difficult period, but it has been continuously decreasing in the past three years. In August of this year, Shanghai's stockpiled yarn reached an unprecedented low level, which is indeed a sign of turning danger into safety.

In the past, Shanghai's yarn industry fell into a difficult situation for many reasons, which have been briefly mentioned before. In addition, expensive cotton and cheap yarn were the industry's fatal wounds. The following is a comparative explanation of the market prices of standard cotton and standard yarn:

An examination of Shanghai cotton prices shows that the average price in 1934 increased by 3% compared to 1933, while yarn prices in the same period fell by 7%. Although cotton prices fell sharply this year, yarn prices also fell accordingly. If 1933 is taken as the base year, yarn prices are still lower than cotton prices, which is a major problem for Shanghai's yarn industry. We need to eliminate the monopoly of raw cotton, improve transportation, and reduce raw cotton freight to find a solution.

As for the current cost price of machine-made cotton yarn, taking the selling price of 16-count Ren Zhong brand yarn at 168 yuan per bale as an example, it can be analyzed as follows: 1. Each bale requires 350 catties of cotton, currently priced at 32 yuan per 100 catties, totaling 110 yuan; 2. Fixed capital and labor: 27 yuan; 3. Factory profit: 8 yuan and 42 fen (factory profit will increase or decrease depending on the rise or fall in yarn prices); 4. Interest: 12 yuan; 5. Unified tax: 8 yuan and 58 fen. However, the cost of transporting cotton yarn from Shanghai to the inland areas is also quite high, depending on the distance, as follows: 1. Shanghai to Nanchang: freight 12 yuan, store profit 5 yuan, totaling 17 yuan; 2. From Nanchang to Linchuan: freight 4 yuan, interest 3 yuan, store profit 3 yuan, totaling 10 yuan, so each bale must be sold at 185 yuan in Nanchang and 195 yuan in Linchuan, otherwise, it will be sold below cost. This calculation of cost price is what those who care about industry and commerce should pay attention to.

The evolution, status, and production and sales of Shanghai's yarn industry have been discussed above. Now, let's measure the prospects based on the Ministry of Finance's new monetary policy. According to the new monetary law recently promulgated by the Ministry of Finance, the purpose is to stop the redemption of paper currency to prevent the outflow of silver, to control exchange rates externally, and to increase prices internally. Since last autumn, overseas silver prices have risen sharply, and domestic prices have been affected, falling relatively, and yarn prices are no exception. If the new monetary policy can proceed in an orderly manner, it may have a good impact on the Shanghai yarn market.

World Illiteracy Statistics: Denmark, Sweden, and Luxembourg Have No Illiteracy 129

Regarding the state of illiteracy in various countries around the world, according to numerous surveys and statistics by domestic and foreign education experts or educational institutions, there is already a rough approximation. Here, the illiteracy rate in various countries is recorded as a percentage: Denmark, Sweden, and Luxembourg have no illiteracy; Switzerland has an illiteracy rate of 0.03%; Germany is the same; the Netherlands has 0.23%; the United Kingdom has 3.7%; Japan has 0.94%; Finland and Norway each have 1%; England has 1.8%; the Union of South Africa has 0.99%; Estonia and Ireland each have 3%; Spain has 3.7%; Austria has 4%; New Zealand has 4.17%; Australia has 1.8%; Australia has 4.3%; the United States has 5%; Canada has 5.7%; Czechoslovakia has 7.7%; France has 8.9%; Belgium has 9.3%; Latvia has 14.72%; Hungary has 15.2%; Newfoundland has 22.7%; Poland has 24.9%; Italy has 27%; Ceylon has 33.3%; Honolulu has 36.3%; Argentina has 37.9%; Uruguay has 39.8%; Ecuador has 40%; Yugoslavia has 43.4%; Lithuania has 44.1%; Bulgaria has 44.5%; Yugoslavia has 49%; Liechtenstein has 49.7%; Cuba has 52.4%; Costa Rica has 52.6%; Puerto Rico, El Salvador, and British Guiana each have 55%; the Philippines has 55.5%; Greece has 57.2%; Bulgaria has 58.4%; Romania has 60.16%; Mexico has 62%; the Federated Malay States has 62.6%; Colombia has 67.52%; Portugal has 68%; the Dominican Republic and Panama each have 70%; Nicaragua has 72%; Venezuela has 72.1%; Russia has 72.4%; Brazil has 75.5%; Syria has 80%; Bolivia has 84%; India has 87.95%; Guatemala has 89.08%; Palestine, Haiti, and Siam each have 90%; Egypt has 91.1%. The average illiteracy rate for the above 60+ countries is 37.7%, and the median is 39.9%. As for China, according to statistics from last year, the illiteracy rate is approximately 66.7%, but due to the active promotion of compulsory education and mass education in recent years, the percentage should be lower.

Guangdong Province Promotes Compulsory Education: Central Government Subsidies for Compulsory Education Expenses Arrive Successively; Fifty Designated Counties to Add Short-Term Elementary Schools 130

The Guangdong Provincial Department of Education recently promoted compulsory education and decided to subsidize impoverished counties to establish short-term elementary schools to accommodate out-of-school children in those counties. It also received approval from the provincial government to allocate funds for subsidies. These subsidized short-term elementary schools have been opened one after another. Recently, the national treasury also subsidized Guangdong Province with compulsory education funds, totaling 30,000 yuan for the three months of July, August, and September, which has already been remitted. Therefore, the Department of Education has also designated 50 counties—Sanshui, Sihui, Guangning, Enping, Heshan, Xinxing, Yunfu, Luoding, Xinyi, Yangchun, Yunan, Deqing, Gaoming, Chixi, Raoping, Dabu, Jiaoling, Wuhua, Puning, Lufeng, Haifeng, Heyuan, Zengcheng, Boluo, Conghua, Longchuan, Pingyuan, Zijin, Huilai, Wuchuan, Suixi, Qinzhou, Yanxian, Wanning, Danxian, Lingao, Qiongdong, Renhua, Shixing, Nanxiong, Lechang, Lianxian, Huaxian, Huazhou, Dianbai, Lianjiang, Dingan, Chengmai, Heshan—to add five short-term elementary schools in each county. The salary for each school principal and teacher is fixed at 35 yuan per month. The following matters requiring attention when opening short-term elementary schools in each county and city have been determined: (1) For each county stipulated to receive subsidies within the measures, regarding the subsidized short-term elementary schools to be opened, in addition to those already opened, the opening fees and office expenses must be carefully planned and reported within fifteen days of receiving the document, according to the stipulated amount, and the school address must be selected. The personnel dispatched to each county should cooperate and quickly prepare for the opening of school. The schools that should be established by the county at its own expense should be established at the latest by the beginning of the next semester. (2) Counties that have not received subsidies must also establish at least five short-term elementary schools within one month of receiving the document, with classes starting at the beginning of the next semester. (3) Each county must, before December of this year, divide the elementary school districts in accordance with the provisions of Chapter 3 of the measures, including the total number of elementary school districts in the county, the number of short-term elementary schools and ordinary elementary schools planned in a certain elementary school district, the number of students to be accommodated, the amount of additional funding to be raised, and the number of classes to be expanded. A detailed plan must be reported to the Department for review. (4) Each county and city must formulate measures for the establishment of short-term elementary schools within one month of receiving the document and report them to the Department for record.

Mr. Wu Zaiyuan, a famous mathematician, devoted himself to education and writing for thirty years. He was proficient in his profession and worked hard and perseveringly. His ambition was not to seek personal comfort, but to serve society and the nation wholeheartedly. Even in his retirement, he worked diligently and fell ill due to accumulated fatigue. He unfortunately passed away on July 21 of this year, leaving behind a desolate situation and orphaned children. Anyone who had ties with Mr. Wu Zaiyuan or admired him is welcome to attend the meeting at that time. Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (9) (4) 137

—Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"Does it hurt, Don?"

"It's a bit bad; but I didn't want to wake you up."

"I'm like an owl, always running around at night. Yes, your foot is really like fire: those bandages need to be wetted again," said the mother owl, flapping her wings to get more cold material and a large bottle of ice water.

"Ah, that's good!" Don let out a long sigh as the soaked cloth was wrapped around his foot again, and he drank once, giving his parched throat a refreshing feeling.

"Now, sleep well, and if you see me again, don't panic, because I'm going to sneak in and take a look again, and give you another cold application."

As dawn approached, she re-entered his room, and found him sleeping soundly. He was unaware when she changed the gauze for him, but the traces of pain on his face gradually faded away, and by the time she left, his face was in an extremely calm state.

The second day was Sunday, and the house was very quiet, so he didn't wake up until noon. Looking around, he saw a small face with an eager expression peering in at the doorway. He stretched out his arms, and Tommy ran straight across the space and fell on the bed, shouting, "My Don has returned!" He held him tightly, and was so happy that he squirmed all over like a little worm. Mrs. Bhaer then came in with breakfast, and Tommy insisted on feeding it to him himself, so he fed him like a child, but since Don wasn't very hungry, he rather liked it.

The Wang Sisters' Performance, Day 2: Lao Lu's Hard-Fought Victory Over Chunqing 141

(Kaifeng Correspondence) The Wang sisters, Chunqing and Chunwei, performed for the second time, starting at 2:00 PM today (the 10th), still at the tennis courts of the New Games. The audience reached the level of the first day. The first match was between the Wang sisters and Tong Zhiren and Chen Jingpan. The two sides were evenly matched and did not give way to each other. In the end, the Wang sisters lost 5-7 due to insufficient stamina. The second match was the singles match between Henan's famous player Lu Xifen and Wang Chunqing. When the male and female players met, they each showed their strengths. Chunqing took the lead and made direct shots into the two corners with great strides. Lao Lu struggled extremely hard, and several times failed to save the ball due to being too tired. Lao Lu took a defensive posture, and Wang attacked Lao Lu with forehand and backhand shots, which won the audience a lot of applause. After Lu won the first game, Wang won two consecutive games. Lu then won two more games, and Wang responded with force, chasing after her. When luck came, she attacked with spin balls and succeeded. After Wang won another game, she gradually ran out of steam. Lu seized the opportunity to attack with long shots and short blocks, winning two consecutive games. Although she barely won 7-5, it was a hard-fought victory. The last match was the mixed doubles between Lu Xifen and Wang Chunwei against Chen Jingpan and Wang Chunqing. Wang and Chen won the first set 6-1, and Wang and Lu won the second set 6-3. The match ended in a tie after each side won one set. Due to the cold wind, the match was ended. Special Issue on Lung Disease

Prevention of Intestinal Tuberculosis 149

— Dr. Shen Zhaoquan

Intestinal tuberculosis (also known as intestinal TB) is the formation of tuberculous nodules on the intestinal mucosa. It often follows from pulmonary tuberculosis. The cause is that patients cannot expectorate phlegm but swallow it into the stomach. Because the sputum of pulmonary tuberculosis patients contains countless aggressive tubercle bacilli, swallowing it into the stomach creates a disease nest where they multiply. However, the acidic gastric juice in the stomach has an antiseptic effect, which can prevent the development of tubercle bacilli. Therefore, in the early stages of pulmonary tuberculosis, when the stomach is still healthy, even if countless tubercle bacilli invade, there is no major problem. However, as the disease slowly progresses, from the first stage to the second stage, and then to the third stage, the body gradually weakens, resistance decreases, and the secretion of gastric juice naturally decreases. The acidic fluid that inhibits tubercle bacilli becomes severely deficient. As a result, the tubercle bacilli in the stomach become active and multiply, and they enter the intestines. The intestines are the place where tubercle bacilli most easily multiply, so the symptoms of intestinal tuberculosis begin to appear.

The symptoms of intestinal tuberculosis are, initially, one or two soft stools per day. Before defecation, there is abdominal pain and a rolling sensation in the abdomen. There is fatigue and weakness, food is not easily digested, and there is often discomfort in the lower right abdomen. After a while, the symptoms become more severe, and the number of bowel movements increases. These are the common symptoms of intestinal tuberculosis. These symptoms persist for a long time and are not easily cured immediately. The diarrheal state is also not severe, with slight diarrhea from time to time. This is a characteristic of intestinal tuberculosis. Therefore, chronic diarrhea in tuberculosis patients should be paid attention to.

Prevention of intestinal tuberculosis An investigation of pulmonary tuberculosis patients shows that most develop intestinal tuberculosis when they reach the second or third stage. The reason is that they swallow their phlegm. Therefore, the prevention method is that pulmonary tuberculosis patients, even in the early stages, must strictly prohibit swallowing phlegm. They should often use a 3% Kali Chlorat solution to gargle and take "Lung Vital" ThithWeal internally, which has antiseptic and bactericidal effects. It can also inhibit abnormal acidic fermentation in the stomach, stimulate appetite, and promote the absorption of nutrients from food. Thus, the patient's nutrition is improved. These few points can be said to have special effects.

Treatment of intestinal tuberculosis The primary cause of lung disease must be treated with all efforts. Taking "Lung Vital" in the early stages can often cure mild cases. If it has reached a severe stage, in addition to taking "Lung Vital" PhithWesl on time, a doctor should be consulted for injections and various physical therapies. At the same time, natural therapies such as fresh air, nutrition, and rest should also be implemented.

Lung Capacity and Health 151

— Dr. Shen Xiangbo

The oxygen that we inhale from the air is only partially exchanged with other gases in the lungs. The other part remains in the lungs. This remaining air is called residual air, and it is about 1200 cubic centimeters. The amount of air inhaled during a normal breath is about 500 cubic centimeters. However, after exhaling the air in the lungs, if one tries harder, one can still exhale a large amount. The amount of air that can be completely exhaled after a normal inhalation, followed by a deep inhalation, is called lung capacity. This amount varies depending on race, individual, age, etc. The average lung capacity of British people is 3700 cubic centimeters. The average lung capacity of Swiss people is 3200 cubic centimeters. The average lung capacity of people of East Asian descent is 3300 cubic centimeters for students and 3930 cubic centimeters for laborers. In general, the stronger the body and the taller the stature, the greater the lung capacity. For ordinary young and middle-aged men of East Asian descent, a lung capacity of 3200 to 3300 cubic centimeters can be considered a strong physique. For women, about three-quarters of that of men, i.e., about 2400 cubic centimeters, can be considered healthy.

Editor's note Those who are infected with tuberculosis are, in fact, prone to lung diseases due to physical weakness and lung weakness—insufficient absorption of oxygen and elimination of carbon dioxide. To prevent this, one must practice deep breathing to improve gas exchange, and it is even more important to take internal medicines to nourish and strengthen the lungs. When I examine people with physical weakness and lung weakness, I always recommend using "Lung Vital" PhithWeal, because this product contains important medicines for strengthening and healing the lungs. Those who are weak can take it to strengthen their body and prevent tuberculosis. Those who are already sick can take it to recover early. I have seen that all those who have taken "Lung Vital" have become physically stronger—with larger lung capacity. Even those who have been diagnosed with tuberculosis by doctors have recovered their health in a short period of time. Because the results of my practical experience are so good, I record them to inform my compatriots.

The Danger of Whooping Cough 155

— Chen Yiqing

Whooping cough is a contagious disease that specifically affects children. It is caused by a microorganism that invades the respiratory system of children. Children under the age of seven are most likely to contract it, and even newborns can suffer from this condition. It is often transmitted through the air, toys, clothing, and utensils. Once a patient appears in a family, the siblings will inevitably be infected one after another. The symptoms of the disease—after an incubation period of two to seven days—present as simple bronchitis symptoms. Coughing lasts for about one to two weeks, followed by paroxysmal spasmodic coughing for about four to five weeks. In mild cases, the attacks occur three to thirty times a day. In severe cases, sixty to a hundred times. Eventually, the attacks gradually decrease, and recovery is possible in two to three weeks. The course typically lasts more than two months and sometimes extends to six or seven months.

When children suffer from this disease, they often develop various complications. The most common is bronchopneumonia. Most children who die from whooping cough do so because of bronchopneumonia. In essence, whooping cough itself does not cause fever. If fever of 38 degrees or higher occurs and persists for two or three days without decreasing, there must be a complication. In addition to bronchopneumonia, attention must also be paid to meningitis, otitis media, and pulmonary emphysema, which often occur concurrently with whooping cough.

When children suffer from whooping cough, hernias may sometimes develop—such as umbilical hernias and inguinal hernias—but these are not life-threatening and should not be feared. After the disease is cured, pulmonary tuberculosis often develops. Children with poor nutrition and glandular disease almost always develop pulmonary tuberculosis after suffering from this disease. Therefore, special attention must be paid during the recovery period of whooping cough. The prevention of whooping cough requires isolation to prevent infection. It is most important that sick children do not come into contact with other children.

The treatment of whooping cough requires careful attention to avoid catching a cold again after the onset of the disease. Choose easily digestible liquid foods that are nutritious. The room should be clean, bright, and well-ventilated. Mental tranquility is essential. All mental stimuli such as joy, anger, fear, and shock, as well as sensory stimuli such as loud sounds and bright lights, should be avoided. Currently, there is no specific medicine for the treatment of this disease. Although there is a whooping cough vaccine injection therapy, its effectiveness is not yet perfect. General physicians treat it by adopting symptomatic treatment, giving cough suppressants and sedatives when coughing attacks occur.

Recently, the medicine "PhithWeal" has been used for whooping cough. It can clear the lungs, relieve coughing, dissolve phlegm into water, reduce inflammation, sterilize, and prevent bronchopneumonia, shortening the course of the disease. Therefore, doctors widely appreciate and use it. The author has also experimented with it many times and found it to be truly effective. Moreover, this product contains no toxic substances and tastes very sweet, making it especially convenient for sick children to take orally.

Whooping cough, in the eyes of ordinary people, may seem insignificant. In fact, the number of deaths is several times higher than that of infectious diseases such as measles. Complications make it even more dangerous. It is especially dangerous for young children. Therefore, it is necessary to take "PhithWeal" as soon as the disease starts and to take great care of oneself to avoid bronchopneumonia.

The course of this disease is very long. Many people die during this time due to physical weakness. Therefore, great attention must be paid to nutritional supplementation during the recovery period. Among the nourishing tonics suitable for children, "Conbour's San-Vl-ta-Ce" is the best and can also prevent the development of pulmonary tuberculosis.

Publishing World

On Speculation in the Publishing Industry 156

— Xu Lü

Some lament the speculation and commercialization in the publishing industry. Publishing is a type of business, and in the modern era of commercial warfare, businesses must speculate to find a way out, make money, and avoid losses. On closer examination, this is an extremely normal phenomenon: the so-called "transformation" is not real, but rather a "true color." Speculation is one of the skills of commerce, one of the skills of true colors. If the publishing industry does not speculate, it is not a business. If it is a business but does not speculate, then publishers can only drink the west wind [i.e., be impoverished].

I am not a publisher; nor am I defending the speculative commercial publishing industry. My point is: in the modern era of commercial warfare, speculation and commerce are both normal terms; to put it bluntly, they are normal behaviors. To criticize the publishing industry with such terms is foolish and inappropriate, equivalent to blaming someone who makes a living by gambling, saying: "Why do you gamble!"

To outsiders, speculation in the publishing industry is indeed abhorrent, damaging the dignity of cultural endeavors, but they themselves see it as extremely ordinary, extremely legitimate. They believe that engagement in the publishing industry, based on commercial forms, can only be this way. Why? Because modern commerce is precisely this way: without speculation, one cannot stand firm.

The current publishing industry is ultimately just a business, and business ultimately requires means.

Therefore, merely cursing the speculation in the publishing industry, while fundamentally correct, is not very suitable for the situation. Cursing speculative publishers for losing their conscience, while fundamentally flawless, does not understand the hardships of those being cursed. To criticize the decline of the publishing industry, one should point out the root of its decline.

The current decline of the publishing industry is obvious and undeniable. So, how did it decline? The publishing industry does not "love" to decline; there is another reason that forces them to decline in this way. This, in a narrow sense, is speculation; but it is also not "love" of speculation, but rather the necessity to speculate under certain circumstances.

This certain circumstance, this reason, in my view, should be attributed to a larger topic: the social and economic recession.

This topic is too big for me to discuss. My intention is merely to speak up for the publishing industry.

When the economic situation is good, the publishing industry will naturally be able to improve and avoid speculation. This is very obvious: we only need to look at how the books published by a few well-capitalized bookstores are more serious and solemn, while the books published by small bookstores are haphazard and careless, to understand.

In such a helpless situation, directly rebuking the publishing industry: "Hey! How dare you speculate!" or shouting: "Hey! No speculation allowed!"... These will not succeed. We can only: on the one hand, hope that the root cause of the social economy will improve, and on the other hand, hope that publishers will retain some conscience within the possible range. We can only hope, not demand—because it is impossible to demand.

But conscience can only exist when there is surplus. The current publishing industry is in dire straits, and it is probably difficult to find anyone willing to discover their conscience. —This is why our publishing industry is helpless!

Speculation means keeping up with the trend. If it is a good trend, then this speculation will be a good phenomenon, because because of everyone's speculation, it will promote the trend to be more lively and broader, that is, to make the publishing industry more prosperous, richer, and more vibrant. But if the trend is bad, speculation can have a bad effect. Because there is so much speculation, the bad trend will become even more rampant, becoming a flood, impossible to clean up.

So speculation is not always bad. Good or bad also depends on the trend. The trend is stimulated by the readers' taste direction. Then, starting from the readers' taste to diagnose and treat the bad situation of speculation, may also be a fundamental method.

This should be the task of educators, critics, and writers. Although the readers' taste direction is also related to speculation; but compared to the above-mentioned "experts," the responsibility of publishers is relatively less.

Regarding the current speculative situation in the publishing industry, I feel that irresponsible educators, critics, and writers not only are not responsible, but also have the power to promote it.

Finally, let's talk about the harms of speculation in principle. In addition to directly promoting bad trends, speculation also has more subtle harms.

For example, take publishing a book. The content of the book caters to the trend. If the trend being catered to is a bad trend, then needless to say, that book is already bad. If the trend being catered to is a good trend, then according to the rules, it should be a good book, but no, it is still a bad book.

The passing of trends is also very fast. Especially in our Chinese "circles." For example, in literature, a trend often lasts for many years in the West, but in China, it only takes a few months. Therefore, for a book to catch up with the trend, or even the highest point of the trend (the highest point of the trend sells the most), it must also be produced equally quickly. The maker of the book must rush to make it, and the publisher must rush to print it, so they only care about speed and not about quality—no, they don't even care about being presentable. As a result, even if the book has a good topic, it is still a mess. The trend is finally caught up with, and readers who are enthusiastic about the trend regard a yellow cow as a horse [i.e., accept something inferior as good], not carefully examining the quality of the content, just reading, just reading, and perhaps even think it is a good book after reading it—because they think it is a "product of the times." The publisher, of course, has earned some money, and when all their attention is focused on money, of course there is no room for "conscience" to appear, completely ignoring what impact that book has on the unfortunate readers.

Speculation on bad trends is of course bad; but speculation on good trends often cannot avoid mistakes: that is, this kind of rough and shoddy production.

The method of diagnosis and treatment is the same as above: to treat the root cause. But on the one hand, it also depends on the three "experts" to fulfill their tasks: educators tell readers "what kind of books are bad books," critics point out "which one is a bad book," and writers make a good one, compare it with the bad one, so that people can clearly see its badness.

Review of Wang Wenru's Edited and Proofread "Complete Works of Gong Ding'an" 157

— Hong Shu

The Complete Works of Gong Ding'an, one of the six famous works of Sinology published by the World Book Company, was popular for a time. But this book is actually the 1909 Guoxue Fulun Society edition, with only a few supplementary notes added on the outside. The former book was titled Edited and Proofread by Hao Haozi, while this book is titled Edited and Proofread by Wang Wenru. Now, the prefaces of the two books are largely identical, suggesting that they are the same person. We have three points to say about this book.

First, the preface by Wang at the beginning of this book states: "During the Jiaqing and Daoguang periods of the Qing Dynasty... Ding'an rose among them... extending to the Tongzhi and Guangxu periods, he was revered as the Gong school... The posthumous collections were circulated and evaluated by several famous scholars... I have seen about dozens of scholars who all could express their insights, compiled and recorded them, but over time, their names have been forgotten." This means that the evaluations in this book were compiled by him. But this is not the case. After Wu Xu's preface in the Guoxue Fulun Society edition, there is the inscription "In May of Yìwèi (1895), Gong Huan's two notes: 'Zhang Junshì combined the three families of Zhu Xinyuan, Sun Qiushi, and Yanghu Zhao Huifu's reading versions for proofreading. Now it is proofread based on Shizhi's version.'" Wang's preface is forty years later. Furthermore, at the end of the sequel, there are three notes titled "Huang Xingyuan's Notes," one of which states: "This is Cheng Pushun's version of the Gong Ding'an Wenji, punctuated by a common scholar. It is recorded from the original engraving of Ding Gong's own notes, with occasional additions, which Jiang Jianxia, a court official, once recorded. Now it is copied again." It can be seen that the compilation of evaluations existed as early as forty years ago with Gong Fuhuan, and Huang Xingyuan (or one and the same person) unknown how many years before 1909, which means that Wang fabricated a lie to deceive people.

The only addition in this book compared to the Guoxue Fulun Society edition is the effort of supplementary notes. This may be Wang's achievement. However, these supplementary notes are of unknown origin and have been arbitrarily altered, which is very wrong. Now, several common examples are summarized as follows:

1. Inappropriate Selection of Materials—This is a common problem throughout Wang's book, that is, he used indirect materials as much as possible. For example, the note on the Inscription for the Spirit Path of Zhuang Gong in the Collected Works, page 278 of the first volume, states: "Wu Changshou said, 'In the year of Wuxu, Zhuang Qing Shan hosted Ding Gong's family, and spoke of the beauty of his ancestor Zhuang Gong Cunyu's deeds, and also said that the inscription was not yet complete. In the year of Jimao, when Ding Gong was in the capital, he met Song Yuting, the grandson of Zhuang Gong's daughter, and again inferred Gong's aspirations, and in that year, less than three days before abandoning human affairs, he gathered all the words and selected the most important ones to write the Inscription for the Spirit Path of Zhuang Gong.'" Wu's words are recorded in his own compiled Chronological Biography, without specifying its basis. Now, Chen Li's handwritten notes on the Collected Early Works of Ding'an reveal that his book contains many of Ding'an's own notes. The Inscription for the Spirit Path of Zhuang Gong entry states: "In the year of Wuyin, the Jiaqing period, Zhuang Jun Shou hosted me in his house, and one evening spoke to me of the beauty of his ancestor's deeds, and also said: 'The inscription is not yet complete.' That evening, Shoujia dreamed of Gong twice, as if he had something to entrust. The next day, Shoujia asked for it. In the year of Jimao, I met Song Xiangfeng, the grandson of Gong's daughter, and Xiangfeng inferred Gong's aspirations in this way for me. In the year of Renwu, less than three days before abandoning human affairs, I gathered all the words and selected the most important ones to repay Gong, Ding'an's own notes." The circulated versions of the Collected Early Works of Ding'an are extremely rare. Wu himself claimed to have "searched and obtained one volume." Then it can be known that what is said in the Chronological Biography is based on Ding'an's own notes. He recorded the year of his writing as "Renwu year, less than three days before the end of the year," so Wu slightly adopted his words and compiled them under the year of Renwu, the Daoguang period, changing "Renwu" to "that year," in order to facilitate the writing and avoid complexity. However, Wang did not notice this and followed his text, which the reader will never understand. Also, Wuxu in Wu's text is the 43rd year of Qianlong, when Ding'an was not yet born, or the 18th year of Daoguang, which is already fifteen years after the Collected Early Works were engraved in the year of Guìwèi in the third year of Daoguang, clearly knowing its mistake. The self-note is "Wuyin" as the 23rd year of Jiaqing, which is exactly five years from the time of writing in Renwu. However, Wang still followed Wu's mistake. Because Ding'an's Collected Early Works are not easy to find, it is understandable to use indirect materials, but there are many that are clearly from this collection, yet he still uses those. For example, the note on the 140th Miscellaneous Poem of the Jihai Year states, "Wu Changshou said, 'Ding Gong once presented the strategy of planting mulberry trees in Beizhi in the north to the senior officials of Ji Fu, and when passing through Suzhou, he presented the strategy of water conservancy in Wuzhong to the Chief Administrator of Lushān. His concern for the people and things was always present.'" Wu's words are based on the original title of the 21st Miscellaneous Poem, "Presenting the strategy of planting mulberry trees in Beizhi in the north to the senior officials of Ji Fu," and the original title of the 140th Miscellaneous Poem, "Presenting the strategy of water conservancy in Wuzhong to the contemporary scholar Yu Lushan, the Chief Administrator." Wang instead quoted his words as a note, not knowing what benefit there is. Wang's supplementary notes mostly take Wu's Chronological Biography as a basis. At the same time, Wu's Chronological Biography mostly takes this collection as its basis. Wang can be said to have mistaken his mother's home.

2. Inappropriate Citation—This can be said to be forced association. For example, the note on the Praise for Zhi Guizi in the Collected Works, page 11 of the second volume, states, "Ding Gong was frustrated and fled to Zen Buddhism, liked Western books, and claimed to have reached deep subtleties, so he wrote this praise." According to Wei Yuan's Ancient Micro Hall Outer Collection, volume three, the preface to Ding'an Wenlu states, "(Ding'an) especially liked Western books in his later years and claimed to have reached deep subtleties." It is clear that Wang's words are a wrong transcription of these two sentences. The year in which the Praise for Zhi Guizi was written is unknown. However, this article has been included in the second volume of Ding'an's Collected Early Works, which shows that although it is not an early work, it was before the third year of Daoguang. At that time, Ding'an was not yet "frustrated and fled to Zen Buddhism," nor did he "claim to have reached deep subtleties." How could it be as Wang said, "therefore he wrote this praise"? Ding'an's later Buddhist achievements are in Ding'an's Separate Collection engraved by Deng Shi. This praise is not qualified to relate to Ding'an's own words.

3. Inappropriate Excerpts—For example, the note on the eighth Miscellaneous Poem states, "Dai Chunshi said: 'This mountain does not speak and looks at the Central Plains, it is truly able to express the feelings of West Mountain.'" According to Dai's words in his own Compiled Idle Talk of the Suffering Studio, volume two, the original text states: "A certain Ministry Official of Gong Ding'an once said to me! 'West Mountain sometimes seems vaguely separated from the outer clouds, and suddenly falls before the desk, regardless of wind, rain, sunshine, or haze.' His poem about West Mountain says: 'This mountain does not speak and looks at the Central Plains,' it is truly able to express the feelings of West Mountain." We read Dai's original text very clearly, but after being cut off by Wang, it is headless and tailless.

Wang's achievements in studying Gong for more than ten years—these supplementary notes can be said to be worthless. Annotation is also a kind of literary criticism (in the broad sense), which is extremely important. However, scientific annotation must be based on textual research, the attitude must be faithful, and the materials must be direct (if there are no direct materials, the entire text should be copied). Unfortunately, Wang's supplementary notes stand on the exact opposite side, so they are the most unscientific and the most unfavorable to scholars' research.

Furthermore, this book's self-proclaimed "complete edition" is also deceiving. If the Complete Works of Gong Ding'an published by the Guoxue Fulun Society in 1909 said this, it would not be an exaggeration at all. But this is the 1935 edition. In these more than twenty years, many posthumous writings have been discovered. As far as I know at this moment, there are two complete sets. One is Ding'an's Separate Collection engraved by Deng Shi (1910), in the Fengyulou Series; the other is Ding'an's Posthumous Works and Outer Chronicles of Ding'an engraved by Zhang Zuliang (1921), in the Juanjinglou Series. And a little earlier, there are Anecdotes of Yú Língshānmín, in the Guoxue Series, which can be compared with the Chronological Biography. Ding'an's Literary Gleanings are mostly his academic essays, which can be included. Other items such as Notes on Duan's Annotations to Shuowen (in the Continued Classics Explained) can also be included. In short, this complete collection adds nothing to the 1909 Guoxue Fulun Society edition and cannot be considered a complete edition.

Bookstore Scenes 158

— Li Hengzhi

(4) General Manager

In various bookstores, the powers and status of the general manager are different, which is determined by the nature of the bookstore's organization. In name, the powers and status of the general manager are supreme in the bookstore, and in practice, although some bookstores are like this, there are also those who are no different from ordinary shop assistants. The reason for this is determined by the way the general manager is produced. If the general manager is the owner of the bookstore, then the general manager's powers are not only supreme, but also last as long as the bookstore. For example, the Li brothers of Beixin, Mr. Zhang of Shanghai Magazine Company, and Mr. Zhang of Kaiming are all owners or founders and concurrently general managers. On the other hand, general managers who are hired entirely—no, who are entirely hired, some have power, while others are very useless. For example, Mr. Shen Zhifang of the former World Book Company, and the deceased Mr. Hong Xuefan of the Modern Book Company, both had great authority in their bookstores, almost no different from those "sole proprietorship owners concurrently serving as general managers." In addition, we know that Mr. Wang Yunwu of the Commercial Press can almost be said to be a "dictator," and the current General Manager Zou of the Life Bookstore also has great power. It is said that at the welcome party for Mr. Zou's return to China, the Life Bookstore colleagues sang "Our General Manager" in unison, a grand occasion unprecedented in the publishing industry. At the same time, there are also many general managers who come without any purpose and leave without any reason. For example, the general manager of the former Crescent Moon Bookstore was replaced almost every few days, and it is often difficult to determine who the current general manager of Huatong is.

The work of each new bookstore has two major parts: one part is publishing books, and the other part is business operations. How to promote business operations is naturally the responsibility of the general manager, but there are some problems with publishing. Apart from those general managers who are useless and have no right to interfere in publishing matters at all, the important reason is that every general manager may not have the same experience in publishing as they do in business operations. I ask, among the general managers of various bookstores, how many can, like Mr. Wang Yunwu, read thousands of books on scientific management abroad in a month? Therefore, there are often disagreements between the general manager and the editor-in-chief, either because the general manager wants to interfere in publishing matters and the editor-in-chief is unwilling, or because the general manager and the editor-in-chief disagree on publishing opinions. Because the general manager is biased towards the "business perspective," while the editor-in-chief may not have any experience in the "business perspective," this is the main point of conflict. (To be continued)

National Products and Small Industries 159

— Yang An

In this industrially backward China, not to mention the lack of development of large industries, even small industries are very immature. Compared with European and American countries, everywhere is a source of shame. I often talk about this with Mr. Chen Diexian, and Mr. Chen is very interested in vigorously promoting it. Recently, Mr. Gu Bingyuan returned to China after inspecting industries in Europe and America, and greatly praised their small industries, which can be described by the eight words "exquisite, delicate, and just right" to describe all the supplies. Mr. Gu brought back many small handicrafts for our national products industry to study, such as kitchen knives, fruit knives, shell removers, degreasers, wrinkle removers, polishers, fire starters, flower makers, and lighting equipment related to clothing, food, housing, and transportation. They all feel novel, exquisite, and small, and the prices are cheap and the applications are especially important. Every dish and utensil is a product of their small industries, and everyone praises and enjoys using them. I think many small objects are easy to imitate. Mr. Gu bought them back to contribute to the national products industry, and his detailed explanations of their uses are especially admirable. For example, a small package of tea and cigarettes is beautifully decorated and accompanied by detailed instructions, explaining the brewing method and effectiveness, which can be sold at a good price. I hope that colleagues in the national products industry, in addition to separately imitating the specialized industries, will also use new patterns and ingenious functions, and each exert their efforts and each specialize in their strengths to create various small crafts to supply social needs, and not allow imported goods to occupy the market. Mr. Zhang Boling said, "Europeans and Americans create, the Japanese imitate, and the Chinese do not create." Now the Japanese have moved from imitation to creation, and will we Chinese continue to stagnate in non-creation, enjoying the finished products of others? How can we face others, how can we deal with ourselves? Comrades who are interested in small industries, hurry up!

The Future of National Goods After Currency Reform 160

— Xuan Wan

The currency reform issue, which had been brewing for a long time, was finally officially implemented on the 4th of this month with an order from the Ministry of Finance. This is a major reform by our government of China's entire economy, and it has the greatest effect of promoting and protecting our national goods industry. It is worthy of our collective attention and a review of its causes and effects by all those engaged in the national goods business.

Because China has always been a country with an import surplus, the international balance of payments can never be balanced. In the end, the only way to pay for it is to use cash, and in recent years, precisely because of the above reasons, silver has been flowing out in torrents, and China's silver reserves are in danger of being exhausted, and the disintegration of the entire national economy has become a matter of time. Therefore, this time, the government resolutely implemented the new currency system, adopting currency issuance and prohibiting the use of cash, precisely to try to manage the currency, stabilize finance, so that silver can be concentrated, and the entire industry and commerce can enter a new stage. In particular, our national goods industry, on the one hand, can have an active trend in export trade due to the reduction of foreign exchange parity, while the import of foreign goods, on the contrary, will increase costs. After that, it will be difficult for them to dump goods in our country's market. On the other hand, due to the unification of paper money issuance and the concentration of reserves, there is no fear of currency contraction, chips can be increased, and credit can be expanded, so that the national goods business can flourish. Other benefits, such as stimulating price increases after the implementation of the new currency system, are also of great benefit to the future of national goods.

However, those of us engaged in the national goods business should not be too optimistic. The future of developing national goods still requires us to proceed with greater prudence. Everyone knows that in the current stage, there are two paths that national goods factories should take. First, we must strive to seize the opportunity to make gradual progress, seek to expand the domestic and foreign markets, promote the progress of export business, and pay attention to the import of foreign goods after the reduction of foreign exchange parity, and compete and deal with them strongly. Because the cost of foreign goods themselves has been raised, in this instance, it is necessary to overthrow their latent power in the Chinese market and replace them with national goods. Second, we must try to use this plan to expand the manufacturers themselves, take advantage of the circulation of currency, the increase of chips, and the expansion of credit, and strive to increase the manufacturers' greater productivity, improve the quality of products, improve sales techniques, and make all equipment more rational.

In short, this currency reform is undoubtedly beneficial to the prosperity of the entire industrial sector, but what is most needed is the efforts of our manufacturers themselves. In this good opportunity, we must strive to develop domestic and foreign markets, improve our own organization, consolidate external credit, and establish the foundation of a strongest national industry.

Promoting National Goods and the Baojia System 161

— Ziming

Recently, Chinese people, in view of the dumping of foreign goods, the bankruptcy of the rural economy, and the critical state of the national economy, have risen up to promote national goods. However, if we examine the past achievements calmly, I am afraid it is difficult to satisfy people! Just because promotion is promotion, foreign goods are still used: this is very painful! However, promoting national goods without a strict organization is also futile. Now the most pressing organization for the people is the Baojia system. If it is used to promote the national goods movement, it will be several times higher than empty talk on paper, right? —Now I will write down the method of using the Baojia system below:

The matter of advocating the use of national goods should be brought up at the Baojia conference for discussion. The implementation methods should be listed in detail. After public discussion and approval, it should be recorded in the Baojia regulations, signed and sealed by the Baojia chief, and the household head should also sign it. It should be hung in a public place and a copy should be submitted to the district office for safekeeping. On the one hand, the Baojia chief should inform the Jia chief of the significance of using national goods and social recovery, and the Jia chief should inform the household head, and the household head should inform the whole family to comply.

On the day when the use of national goods begins, the Baojia chiefs of each township should hold a joint oath-taking ceremony, guided by the district chief and supervised by the county chief. At the same time, the public is welcome to participate. After taking the oath, in addition to the household head guaranteeing to the Jia chief, the Jia chief to the Baojia chief, the Baojia chief to the township chief, and the township chief to the district chief that they will not use foreign goods, they must also provide mutual guarantee documents to supervise each other. Once a deliberate violation is found, it should be immediately reported to the district level for the most severe punishment.

The staff of the district office should set an example and use national goods: another national goods inspector should be sent to various places at any time to investigate and guide. I think that this method, if implemented with determination, will definitely be effective!

Our Country's Paper Windows Can Transmit Ultraviolet Rays 162

— Shen Chengzhao

In the early autumn of this year, several experts in electro-optics among the members of the Mechanical Research Association of New York City, USA, specially studied the paper windows of old-style buildings in our country. The results proved that this kind of paper windows is very suitable for scientific use, because it can transmit ultraviolet rays in the sun. This kind of ultraviolet rays gives us great benefits. According to Mohr's test, if some oil is applied to the paper window, the transmittance of ultraviolet rays is stronger. Now most of the lung disease sanatoriums in the United States have switched to using paper windows from our country.

A Visit to the China Nail Manufacturing Company 163

— Xian

It is shameful to say that we cannot even provide ourselves with a nail, and we need to rely on imports, and a large amount of money flows to foreign countries. What a shameful thing this is! According to the Customs report last year, in addition to those manufactured by foreigners in factories in our country, the import of round nails reached more than 240,000 barrels. Countrymen, pay attention! Don't despise it just because you can buy a few for a copper plate.

The China Nail Manufacturing Company was founded in November of the 20th year. Its progress is faster than that of ordinary factories, and it is worth visiting. The factory is located on Funing Road, Yangshupu. Manager Qian Junxiang studied in the United States for many years and specialized in machinery. After returning to China, he organized the factory with his friend Mr. Ye and others. They have been working hard for five years.

In terms of equipment, there are currently sixteen nail making machines, which can produce eighty barrels of round nails (commonly known as foreign nails) per ten hours (each barrel weighing 100 pounds). The nails produced have the following advantages: (1) The nail head is round and neat, and the thickness is appropriate; (2) The nail teeth are deeply cut and firmly secured; (3) The nail body is straight; (4) The nail tip is sharp and easy to enter the wood. In addition to nail making, the factory also has eight wire drawing machines, which draw coarse wire into thin wire for nail making, which can greatly reduce costs. There is also a paper clip machine. In the future, we will have domestic paper clips to use, and we will no longer need to rely on imports. It is said that it is sold by the China National Goods Company for one dime per box. There is also a barbed wire machine, which specializes in manufacturing iron wire products.

In this year of national goods, it is indeed commendable that such excellent national goods are available, so I am happy to introduce them.

Recently, there has been much discussion in the market regarding the export of Chinese cotton. Therefore, the cotton market is exceptionally firm, and bullish traders are aggressively pushing up prices. In addition, recent estimates of American cotton have been reduced by more than 300,000 bales, leading to a continuous increase of 65 points, making market sentiment even firmer. Indian cotton is also following suit. According to reliable sources, yesterday, Dong Cotton, Nissin, Jiangshang, Yinghua, and other foreign firms transacted 15,000 dan of Shanghai cotton at a price of 50 yuan (Japanese currency) and 5,000 dan of Tongzhou cotton at a price of 52 yuan (Japanese currency). All were baled and shipped to Japan. This has made speculators even more eager to hoard, and market prices are rising steadily, resulting in a daily trend of rising prices with no declines. It is found that on November 4, the highest peak of the December contract of raw cotton futures was 43 yuan, and today's closing price is 42 yuan and 5 cents, only 9.5 cents different. On the same day, the highest peak of the December contract of spun yarn futures reached 204 yuan, and today's closing price is 193 yuan and 2 corners, still 10 yuan and 8 corners short. It can be seen that the gap between cotton and yarn prices is widening, and the cost of cotton yarn is continuously increasing. Yarn sales remain weak, and manufacturers are finding it particularly difficult.

Although trading was not very active, market prices rose quietly. Near-term contracts such as November and December rose by as much as $0.10 compared to the market at the beginning of the week, and January and February contracts rose by $0.07 to $0.08.

In the afternoon session, the initial factor was the decline in the flour market, which dampened market sentiment. Then, rumors spread that factories had ordered foreign wheat at a price of 6.6 yuan, causing widespread fear. Everyone sought to sell, and market prices plunged by about $0.10. To safeguard the people's food supply, it is necessary to encourage these purchases, which will naturally ease market sentiment.

A General Discussion on Spermatorrhea 190

— (Physician Zhou Kechang)

Spermatorrhea refers to the involuntary leakage of semen, often triggered by nightmares during the early morning hours. After the emission, one experiences fatigue, headache, dizziness, heart palpitations, mental distress, and weakness in the legs. In severe cases, it can occur during the day, triggered by imagining lewd things or viewing obscene books and paintings. In even more severe cases, sexual desire gradually decreases, the ability to achieve an erection weakens, and the frequency of spermatorrhea increases, eventually leading to neurasthenia (nervous exhaustion). The causes of spermatorrhea are generally excessive sexual activity, masturbation, and other conditions such as chronic gonorrhea, prostatitis, and cystitis. Therefore, prevention requires strict abstinence from masturbation, moderation in sexual activity, avoidance of physical and mental overexertion, avoidance of alcohol and irritating foods, and the use of light and soft bedding at night. Regular cold water rubs on the genitals are also beneficial. As for medication, "Heierbang" pills are both effective and harmless. I have seen many patients recover after taking this medication.
