Commentary

From "Lack of Butter" to "Acquiring New Territory" 194

— Fang Yin

According to reports, German Economic Minister Schacht recently delivered a speech in which he stated:

"The current scarcity of butter in Germany is a matter of great concern. It should be understood that if our country's exports cannot be increased, then domestic daily necessities cannot be supplied. Our country cannot forever endure this suffering and should be understood by foreign people. The solution lies in increasing domestic production and acquiring new territory where we can obtain the raw materials we need. Therefore, the mere lack of butter is enough to prove the legitimacy of our demands."

At a time when the global economic crisis is intensifying, it is not surprising that imperialists seek to resolve their own crises by obtaining raw material supply bases and new markets. However, after the European War, all the world's colonies have been divided. Germany is a defeated nation, and its former territories have been seized by the victorious powers. Therefore, as the economic crisis worsens, it naturally feels most acutely the lack of foreign markets and raw material supply bases. Schacht's remarks were undoubtedly made for this reason. However, we cannot help but immediately think that if Germany can demand "new territory" for the "lack of butter," then other countries may also demand "new territory" for other deficiencies. But whose territory should be included in whose "new territory"? I think, apart from another massacre, there will probably be no other new tricks.

However, the victims of this conflict will naturally not be any imperialist powers themselves, but rather the weak nations and innocent laborers, because only they will be used as cannon fodder and meat for the slaughter.

On the seventeenth anniversary of the end of the European War, hearing Schacht's remarks could not help but evoke the brutal memories of the European War.

Vegetable Boat 195

— Fang Zhou

The early morning market lay shrouded in the dim light of dawn. Gen Sheng and his wife, however, had already left their warm blankets at the third crow of the morning rooster. Gen Sheng, with a roll of grayish-white canvas in hand, walked towards the riverbank at the stone bridgehead. His wife, carrying a food basket and shouldering an oar, followed Gen Sheng to their old, partially damaged boat. After a brief tidy-up, Gen Sheng jumped ashore and called out to set sail, while she started the fire in the galley to cook breakfast.

The small town was still quiet. Only a blacksmith's shop at the edge of town had an apprentice yawning and lazily removing the dilapidated planks of the door, one by one. Although the doors of a few teahouses were already open, apart from the waiters groaning and puffing as they pumped the bellows to light the stoves, the wooden tables remained silent, showing no sign of the bustling activity that would come in an hour.

"Vegetable boat departing! Vegetable boat to Xishan departing!" Gen Sheng shouted twice through the alleys before returning to the boat to sit at the stern, sipping hot tea and smoking his cheap tobacco, waiting.

At this time, the small barges and cargo ships moored in the river still had their awnings tightly covered, as if no one lived there. The awnings were covered in a layer of frost, as white as if a light snow had fallen overnight. No one could be seen washing clothes on the river wharves either.

The sky gradually brightened, and the thick fog slowly dissipated. The peaks of Huachuan Ridge emerged from the milky white mist.

Soon, vegetable sellers began to arrive, one after another, carrying shoulder poles loaded with various vegetables: local produce, market goods, green vegetables, radishes, taro, scallions, garlic, as well as fish and meat. They rested their loads, lifting them to hand over to Gen Sheng. Gen Sheng's wife also helped to load the baskets and crates into the large central hold until it was full. Then the people hopped aboard, one by one, tossing their carrying poles into the hold. The boat rocked back and forth from the sudden weight, forcing people to hold onto each other to avoid falling into the water!

This small boat had a limited capacity, but now it was loaded with more than ten shoulder-loads of vegetables and over ten people. As a result, the gunwale was only three inches above the waterline. Any lower and water would seep into the hold.

Once everyone was on board, a clamor of voices arose. Some pulled out wrinkled, low-quality cigarettes from their chests, while others hastily used the corner of their skirts to wipe the sweat from their foreheads, which continued to steam as if they had just come out of a steamer. The previously quiet surroundings were now full of life.

"Is everyone here? We should set sail," Zhang Axing asked Gen Sheng, as much a question as a prompt.

"Why hasn't A-Jin come yet? Doesn't he always come?" Gen Sheng's wife remembered how many people usually took the boat. She looked around the passengers and realized one person was missing. After thinking for a moment, she realized it was A-Jin, the dry goods merchant, who hadn't arrived. So, she asked the Two-Headed Monk this question.

"He's not coming. His wife gave birth last night!" the Two-Headed Monk replied in a peculiar tone.

"She gave birth? To what?" This was A-Jin's wife's uncle, so he asked with concern.

"I heard it was a boy! — But the mother is not doing well."

Gen Sheng went ashore to unlock the chain securing the boat to the wild mulberry tree. He returned, stowed the gangplank, and lightly tapped the stone bank with his pole a couple of times, causing the boat to swing into the center of the river. He took his pole and pushed off a few more times. The boat seemed to obey his command, heading towards the river mouth. He stowed the pole, busily stepped over to lower the rudder on the right side, then walked to the stern to help his wife with the oar.

Once they were out of the mouth of the river, they noticed that the southeast wind was quite strong. They released the rudder, raised the grayish-white canvas sail, and let it drift with the wind.

The dozen or so vegetable merchants sat in rows along both sides of the boat's gunwale. Gen Sheng leaned leisurely against the tiller, drinking his liquor.

To the east of Tai Lake, the morning sun gradually emerged from the horizon, like a red egg rolling upward. A gentle breeze blew through the sail, propelling the boat faster.

The towering peak of Dongting Xishan had begun to exhale wisps of white smoke. They knew that the people of Xishan were also cooking breakfast. Then the long bank of Zhenxia Harbor slowly crept past the boat.

A Night in Xuzhou 196

— Meng Hua

We were travelling on a military vehicle this time, originally expecting to arrive in Xuzhou by noon that day, and then transfer to a train to Bengbu, where we would stay for a day or two. However, before the train even reached Xuzhou, the woods outside the window had merged with the twilight. Naturally, the train to Bengbu had already left, so we had no choice but to spend the night in Xuzhou.

Carrying our simple luggage, we walked along a gravel road and finally settled in a cheap inn. The innkeeper was busy bringing us water, unpacking our bedding, and making tea, while also chattering away, mostly about irrelevant things. After taking care of everything, he smiled ingratiatingly at my friend (who was a military officer) and said:

"Sir, haha, you must be tired after a long day, do you want me to get you a girl?" He deliberately let his awkward laughter cover up the rest of his sentence, naturally giving us a speculative look.

"We'll talk about it later," my friend said, dismissing him, and then turning to me, "There are so many brothels in Xuzhou." He tapped the heel of his riding boot, seemingly very familiar with the place. "There are really too many, because this is where the Longhai and Jinpu railways intersect. Every day, countless soldiers have to come here and leave from here." He was an "Xuzhou expert," having been to Xuzhou seven or eight times before.

I listened curiously as he described everything about the brothels here, and I also recalled the women dressed in flamboyant clothes and covered in perfume that I had seen on the road just now.

"That's right, those are the prostitutes," my friend said. "Many are girls from Jiangbei, with straightforward personalities, but not as lively as those from the South."

My friend was someone who had narrowly escaped death several times, so he was always cold and indifferent, with no sympathy for anything. Naturally, he had also "played" with those so-called "girls" many times.

We were talking animatedly when suddenly someone stopped outside the door. A silhouette appeared on the glass door. Then the door opened gently, and a slender woman walked in.

"Sir, would you like a song?" She lowered her head, absently twisting the handkerchief in her hands, her voice was gloomy and trembling. After a while, she raised her head again, and with a cold! not begging, gaze swept over the two of us, and said softly, "Sir, what song would you like?"

Her face was very pale, and in the dim light of the small inn, her frail face resembled a fading white rose. My friend seemed stunned by her rare demeanor. After a long while, he slowly said, "No, thank you."

She paused for a moment, then withdrew the hand resting on the table and quietly retreated. Her figure was like a ghost in the darkness, and then disappeared outside the door.

My friend had been in the process of taking off his riding boots, but at this moment, he was also a little dazed, muttering to himself absentmindedly, "This girl is a bit strange! This girl is a bit strange!"

"She's probably a girl who's just starting out," he then said to me. "Shy and timid. You can tell from her appearance. Otherwise, I think playing with her would also... Never mind, never mind, let's get up at seven o'clock tomorrow. If you wake up earlier, don't forget to wake me up."

"When the Weather is Good, the Sun Rises" 197

— Shi Weizhi

Living in these prosperous times, how should one conduct oneself? This question has lingered in my mind for a long time, but I have never been able to decide. Perhaps the reason for my indecision is that I have considered it too thoroughly, feeling that nothing works, and as a result, I cannot help but feel lost.

For example, Mr. Xu Xizhen's "clown" attitude of "when the weather is good, the sun rises," which is "attentive to everyone and avoids offending anyone," is an excellent approach, but "after all the talking, the result is still the same as not saying anything." I dare not raise my hand in agreement with this so-called "smoothness" that "results in saying nothing." "Slickness" may be useful as part of a way to deal with the world, but if one is always smooth and "after all the talking, the result is still the same as not saying anything," then without sacrificing one's own principles, there is no way to solve anything.

In fact, even if one is willing to sacrifice one's own principles, it is not necessarily possible to be "attentive to everyone." Let's take an old example: regarding the purpose of art, there were two schools of thought in the past: "art for art's sake" and "art for life's sake." Which of these two is correct? But to be "attentive to everyone" is difficult. If you say "art for art's sake" is correct, then you cannot be "attentive" to those who advocate "art for life's sake," and vice versa. Saying that neither is correct is something one dare not say or even mention. Saying that both are correct is a way to please no one, and the result is still "offending" someone.

Therefore, "when the weather is good, the sun rises; when it rains, the steps get wet" can only become a clown's interjection on stage.

Moreover, the clown's interjections on stage, at most, are just making a funny face to make the ladies and gentlemen in the audience laugh for a while, thinking that he is still sensible and not annoying. There is no better feeling than this. It is not like "upright speech," which, while lengthy and causing headaches, sometimes makes the ladies and gentlemen more difficult to forget.

Of course, the "lengthy speech" of "upright speech" is just that, a "lengthy speech," and does little to help the actual situation. The ones who really get things done are the "warriors" who hold the command arrows, or the "strategists" who, although "unable to truss a chicken," have military force as their backing. However, compared to the "clown," they are sometimes valued much more by the audience, even though the "clown" has the "funny face" that is "attentive to everyone."

The Temple of Great Peace 198

— Si Quan

This small town has no wharf for night boats to reach the county seat, and to travel by land, one must detour through the neighboring town. In military terms, it is a strategic location: easy to defend when entering, and easy to attack when leaving. However, in terms of agriculture, it is the most disadvantageous place. Even if the land here is sold at the lowest price, no one dares to risk buying it cheaply. Because the rice produced has to be transported to the county seat by human labor, and the journey is so long that even if one sets out in the morning, one probably won't reach halfway by night. If the villagers refuse to pay the rent, only the landlord will suffer.

For generations, this small town has been populated by independent farmers. As for whether they resisted the landlords or bought the land, it is impossible to determine. This secluded town, like a primitive tribe, is closed off and does not interact with the outside world. However, every spring, the Great Peace Temple on this town raises funds for a community event. The temple is called Great Peace, and the meaning of the event is, of course, to ensure the town's peace for the year. It is said that the Great Peace God is truly responsive to prayers. This town is located higher than the neighboring towns, and as a result, regardless of drought or flood in other towns, this place always has a good harvest. The townspeople say that it is due to the power of the Great Peace God. Therefore, when the community event is held each year, foolish men and women who want to share in the power of the Great Peace God are willing to travel for two days, enduring the hardships of the journey, to participate in this "Great Peace Festival." Moreover, they are respectful and reverent, and before setting out, they must fast and bathe, and abstain from meat for three days. Even married couples must sleep separately on the road. From this, one can see the prestige of the Great Peace Temple in this area.

However, if you go to visit this Great Peace Temple with the grand ambition of a sightseer, you will be greatly disappointed. The temple is a dilapidated house that is about to collapse, without a temple gate. An elderly caretaker lives with the Great Peace God, whose clay has already been exposed. Stepping into the temple, the room where the Great Peace God sits in the center is called the hall. Looking up, you can see the sky through several places in the roof beams. And all the accessories belonging to the temple, such as the bailiffs, the "avoidance" and "silence" signs, are all missing. Only the Great Peace God sits in the center (because the central roof beam is intact, otherwise, I think they would have asked him to move to a corner of the room covered in cobwebs). In front of him is a half-table with one leg missing, and a censer. Besides that, there is only the caretaker, crouching at the feet of the Great Peace God like a hungry dog.

When the community event is held, the Great Peace God is clamped to two thick bamboo poles, and two strong farmers run along the entire town as if they are stealing him from the temple. Visitors who have come from afar to share in the power of the Great Peace God also sprint after them, which is called "chasing Great Peace." The caretaker's livelihood depends on the "chasing Great Peace" ritual each year, because the incense money is quite substantial.

The Great Peace God and the caretaker enjoy this Great Peace broth every year, until a war breaks out. When the troops occupy the town, this deity and the Great Peace Temple are destroyed by artillery fire. When the town's farmers return after the war, only the elderly caretaker is missing. It is feared that he also sacrificed himself for the Great Peace God, with whom he depended on for life.

Now there is not a trace of the Great Peace Temple in this town. The boundless rice fields, in these years when various provinces and counties are suffering from severe floods and droughts, the town still has a good harvest every year. Naturally, the power of the Great Peace God has faded from their memories. However, when neighboring towns suffer disasters, they say it is because they have not rebuilt the Great Peace Temple.

A Scene of Utter Desolation

Society is so licentious, people's hearts are so decadent, look up, a scene of utter desolation! The room is filled with color, the room is filled with the aroma of meat, how many young people are buried!

Having hands but not working is like having no hands; demon palace! My husband, buried alive by you! Having legs but not striving upwards is like having no legs; my husband, buried alive by you! Neon lights, dazzling and brilliant, anesthetized his heart; the fragrance of wine, the aroma of flesh, blinded his ambition; lost, all hope; brought back, a heavy burden of resentment and remorse; look up, a scene of utter desolation, lower your head, a desolate landscape everywhere.

Having a brain but not thinking is like having no brain; without a brain, like a cripple, everything becomes hopeless! Having strength but not working is like being crippled and paralyzed; only enjoying pleasure! Cannot last long, a lifetime of only sorrow! Love songs echoing, seductive tunes melodious, covering his thoughts; the flying eyebrows, the unrestrained colors, buried his strength; young people! The country is in great difficulty; this is not a time for singing and dancing! Young people! Open your eyes and take a look, a scene of utter desolation!

"Hero of the Times" is a Problem Play 204

...Deserves Attention

The entire period experienced by the play "Hero of the Times" occupies two major records in world history:

1. World War I.

2. The world-shaking storm of aggression.

Of course, many heroes can be created in the dynamic of these two major records; however, the play depicts not heroes on the battlefield, but heroes in the business world. The entire play begins by writing about how this hero succeeds due to the times, and continues to write until this hero fails due to the times.

Continued on Page 3

Page 19

"The stage is a weapon" (StageIs 00h). This is a metaphor used by people in other countries who value drama. Then, those who are working hard in drama, holding this weapon, should study how to use this weapon well. The purpose of using this weapon well is to ensure that the performance of drama can provide guidance to the masses and benefit society and the country. We made "Hero of the Times" and "Triumphant Song" with the above goals in mind.

The collapse of China's rural areas and the decline of industry and commerce have become undeniable facts. This is a major economic problem in China, and also a major problem for the survival of the Chinese nation. If there is no way to solve this major problem, even if China can escape death from the oppression of cannon fire and iron hooves, it will inevitably die from economic oppression.

"Hero of the Times" is a problem play belonging to the industrial and commercial sector. This problem play contains two reasons: The first reason is to show the result of national capital being oppressed by international capital. The second reason is to show the suicide of the invisible internal war in the psychology of the Chinese people. —Huideng Bank oppresses Zhenxing Yarn Factory, Sun Zhonggui oppresses Zhao Dexiong.

The reasons included in the problem of why China's industry and commerce are declining are, of course, very complicated. It is definitely not just the two reasons played out in the drama "Hero of the Times". However, to save industry and commerce, and to revive industry and commerce, all kinds of reasons must be solved in every way. We held onto the above two reasons and made the problem play "Hero of the Times," hoping to use this problem play to stimulate the masses in order to seek answers in the public's psychology.

Now we want to make further efforts to solicit opinions on solving the problem as material for making the sequel to "Hero of the Times." We sincerely hope that the industrial and commercial sectors, the education sector, and the intellectual class who have suffered pain are willing to generously give us their opinions, and especially hope to have scripts that can solve problems and encourage self-awareness. So that we can use the weapon that is bigger than the stage to benefit the country and society.

We should understand that the initial control of the world's population and all rights belonged to military force, then to culture, and now to economics. If we only shout the slogans of collapse or decline for defense against aggression and the construction of productive bases – industry and commerce – without giving instructions to awaken self-awareness and encourage competition, and sit idly by and watch them be destroyed again, this is driving the people in the bases to do the tragic work of suicide for themselves, for their careers, and for their country.

The realization of this kind of tragic fact is, of course, something that everyone is unwilling to see, and even more unwilling to let this tragic fact become a factor in changing the map, sitting idly by as the country falls into a state worse than India and Korea.

We hope that our calls can gain the sympathy of an audience that goes beyond entertainment, and gain more of the sympathy of audiences who express their opinions to us.

About "Boat Girl" 205

"Boat Girl," written and directed by Shen Xiling, depicts the tragedy and comedy of the women's liberation movement. It has the charm of "Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio" and the meaning of improving society. It is a worthy masterpiece that deserves attention. It has now been sent to Beijing for review, and will be available to the audience as soon as it is approved.

In "Boat Girl," written and directed by Shen Xiling, he introduced the beauty of West Lake from the most beautiful angle and with the most artistic perspective, opening the eyes. The ripples in West Lake, the hazy willows, the six bridges and three temples, the Su Causeway and Broken Bridge, the scenic spots in the lake, combined with the joys and sorrows of human life, are truly a lyrical poem and a sketch painting.

"Boat Girl" is the first collaboration between Lao Gao and Xu Lai. Lao Gao plays the weaver Tie Er, and Xu plays the boat girl A Ling. It can be said that the personalities of these two characters could not be more suitable for Lao Gao and Xu Lai. You see them laughing, sighing, and silently shedding tears on the screen, and you will unconsciously laugh and cry with them, as if the characters on the screen are you yourself. Their expressions in "Boat Girl" have simply reached a state of selflessness. Especially Xu Lai, "She has never done such a good play!" That's what people who have seen the test screenings said.

Joint Film News 206

Since its merger with Twentieth Century Company, Fox Film Corporation has become even more powerful. Their film "Bachelor Bait" is currently showing at the Grand Theater, and "Dressed to Thrill," starring the famous European and American actress Dorothy Lamour and Clive Brook, will be released at the Cathay Theater starting today (Thursday). This is a witty and interesting romance that tells the story of a man who simultaneously falls in love with a modest young woman and a theater star, only to discover that they are one and the same person, leading to a series of amusing incidents.

The first day of the screening of "Bachelor Bait" at the Grand Theater was completely sold out. The sole reason for this is due to the technological advancements in the film itself, completed with sound and better photography. Compared to the era of silent films a decade ago, it naturally has more appealing qualities. However, it is said that because Paramount's musical extravaganza "Hollywood Party" has already been scheduled to be screened from tomorrow (Friday), "Bachelor Bait" can only be shown until today. Friends who love such moral tragedies should not miss this last opportunity.

Warner Bros. spared no effort in producing Shakespeare's famous play "A Midsummer Night's Dream," a prestigious work by the authoritative stage director Max Reinhardt, who joined the film industry for the first time. Movie fans have long yearned for this film. Now, there is excellent news to report to readers: this film will be presented at the Cathay Theater within the month. It is said that when this film was shown in New York, the ticket price was as high as eleven US dollars, and the crowded attendance still broke records. Therefore, when the Cathay Theater screens this film, it may also slightly increase the ticket price.
